Welcome to your comprehensive revision hub. This isn't just a textbook;
it's a \textbf{living document} designed to evolve with you as we move
toward your final MYP 5 assessments.

\part{Algebra}

\chapter{Unit 1: Operations}\label{unit-1-operations}

\section{🎯 Learning Targets}\label{learning-targets}

LT1

Calculate with Integers

Add, subtract, multiply, and divide positive and negative numbers
accurately.

{Positive \& negative} {Four operations} {Number line}

LT2

Apply Order of Operations

Evaluate numerical expressions using BODMAS, including brackets and
exponents.

{BODMAS} {Brackets} {Exponents}

LT3

Operate with Fractions

Add, subtract, multiply, and divide fractions and mixed numbers
fluently.

{LCD} {Mixed numbers} {Simplify}

LT4

Work with Decimals

Perform calculations with decimals and convert between fractions,
decimals, and percentages.

{Decimal operations} {FDP conversion} {Rounding}

LT5

Simplify Complex Calculations

Combine integers, fractions, and decimals in multi-step numerical
problems.

{Multi-step} {Mixed types} {Problem solving}

\section{🗂️ Recall: Formula Card}\label{recall-formula-card}

\subsection*{Essential Operation Rules}\label{essential-operation-rules}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Essential Operation Rules}

\subsubsection*{Simplifying Fractions}\label{simplifying-fractions}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Simplifying Fractions}

\textbf{💡 Pro Tip} A fraction is fully simplified when GCF = 1

\textbf{How to Simplify}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Find the Greatest Common Factor (GCF) of numerator and denominator
\item
  Divide both top and bottom by the GCF
\end{enumerate}

\[\frac{a}{b} = \frac{a \div \text{GCF}}{b \div \text{GCF}}\]

\textbf{Examples}: -
\(\frac{12}{18} = \frac{12 \div 6}{18 \div 6} = \frac{2}{3}\) -
\(\frac{15}{25} = \frac{15 \div 5}{25 \div 5} = \frac{3}{5}\)

\subsubsection*{Rules of Signs (Multiplication \&
Division)}\label{rules-of-signs-multiplication-division}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Rules of Signs (Multiplication \&
Division)}

\textbf{🎯 Memory Trick} Same signs = Happy (+)\\
Different signs = Sad (-)

\textbf{Same Signs → Positive} - \((+) \times (+) = (+)\) -
\((-) \times (-) = (+)\)

\textbf{Different Signs → Negative} - \((+) \times (-) = (-)\) -
\((-) \times (+) = (-)\)

\subsubsection*{Adding/Subtracting
Fractions}\label{addingsubtracting-fractions}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Adding/Subtracting Fractions}

\textbf{⚠️ Common Mistake} Don't add denominators!\\
WRONG: \(\frac{1}{2} + \frac{1}{3} = \frac{2}{5}\)

\textbf{Same Denominator}: Keep denominator, add/subtract numerators
\[\frac{a}{c} + \frac{b}{c} = \frac{a + b}{c}\]

\subsubsection*{Multiplying \& Dividing
Fractions}\label{multiplying-dividing-fractions}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Multiplying \& Dividing Fractions}

\textbf{📝 Quick Method} Cancel BEFORE you multiply - saves time!

\textbf{Multiply}:
\(\frac{a}{b} \times \frac{c}{d} = \frac{a \times c}{b \times d}\)

\textbf{Divide (Keep-Change-Flip)}:
\(\frac{a}{b} \div \frac{c}{d} = \frac{a}{b} \times \frac{d}{c}\)

\subsubsection*{Order of Operations
(PEMDAS/BODMAS)}\label{order-of-operations-pemdasbodmas}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Order of Operations
(PEMDAS/BODMAS)}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{P}arentheses / \textbf{B}rackets
\item
  \textbf{E}xponents / \textbf{O}rders
\item
  \textbf{M/D} Multiplication \& Division (Left to Right)
\item
  \textbf{A/S} Addition \& Subtraction (Left to Right)
\end{enumerate}

\section{📝 Practice Problems}\label{practice-problems}

\subsection{🟢 Easy}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-important-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-important-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title={Guidance}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Read each question carefully before you begin answering it.
\item
  Check your answers seem right.
\item
  Always show your workings.
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{exercise}[Conversion
Table]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u1-conv-table}{}\label{exr-u1-conv-table}

Complete the following table:

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lll@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Fraction & Decimal & Percentage \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\(\frac{1}{2}\) & \ldots{} & \ldots{} \\
\ldots{} & 0.75 & 75\% \\
\end{longtable}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Row 1:} \(\frac{1}{2} = 0.5 = \mathbf{50\%}\)
\item
  \textbf{Row 2:} \(\mathbf{\frac{3}{4}} = 0.75 = 75\%\)
\end{itemize}

\end{tcolorbox}

{Topic: Conversion Table} {Skills: Basic Conversions}

\end{exercise}

∑ × π ÷ √ ◆ ∞ ± ∫ ≠ Δ

\begin{exercise}[Basic
Conversions]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u1-basic-conv}{}\label{exr-u1-basic-conv}

~

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  Write 20\% as a decimal.\\
\item
  Write 9\% as a fraction.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  \(20 \div 100 = \mathbf{0.2}\)\\
\item
  \(\mathbf{\frac{9}{100}}\)
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

{Topic: Basic Conversions} {Skills: Percentage-to-Decimal/Fraction}

\end{exercise}

∑ × π ÷ √ ◆ ∞ ± ∫ ≠ Δ

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-important-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-important-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title={Level 1: Basic Operations}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

Calculate

\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\centering\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2500}}
  >{\centering\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2500}}
  >{\centering\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2500}}
  >{\centering\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2500}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\centering
a
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\centering
b
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\centering
c
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\centering
d
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\(\frac{3}{4}\) of 36 & \(\frac{1}{3}\) of 24 & \(\frac{2}{5}\) of 35 &
\(\frac{4}{9}\) of 72 \\
\end{longtable}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  \((36 \div 4) \times 3 = 27\)\\
\item
  \((24 \div 3) \times 1 = 8\)\\
\item
  \((35 \div 5) \times 2 = 14\)\\
\item
  \((72 \div 9) \times 4 = 32\)
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

{Topic: Fractions of Amounts} {Skills: Multiplicative Reasoning}

∑ × π ÷ √ ◆ ∞ ± ∫ ≠ Δ

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-important-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-important-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title={Level 2: Applied Context}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{Calculate:}\\
a) Zaid earns 800 QAR a month. He spends \(\frac{1}{4}\) on rent and
\(\frac{2}{5}\) on food. How much money does he have left?\\
b) Fatima is buying shoes that normally cost 200 QAR. They are
\(\frac{1}{5}\) off. What is the sale price?\\
c) Amir has 300 marbles. He gives \(\frac{1}{2}\) to his brother and
\(\frac{1}{3}\) of the remaining marbles to his friend. How many does he
keep?

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\item
  Rent: \((800 \div 4) \times 1 = 200\)\\
  Food: \((800 \div 5) \times 2 = 320\)\\
  Total spent: \(200 + 320 = 520\)\\
  Left: \(800 - 520 = 280\) QAR
\item
  Discount: \((200 \div 5) \times 1 = 40\)\\
  Sale Price: \(200 - 40 = 160\) QAR
\item
  To brother: \(300 \times \frac{1}{2} = 150\)\\
  Remaining: \(150\)\\
  To friend: \(150 \times \frac{1}{3} = 50\)\\
  Kept: \(150 - 50 = 100\)
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

{Topic: Fractions of Amounts}\\
{Skills: Word Problems}

\subsection{🟡 Medium}

\begin{exercise}[Time and
Fractions]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u1-time-frac}{}\label{exr-u1-time-frac}

A train is late. It should arrive at 5 pm but arrives at 5:15 pm.

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  How many minutes late is the train?\\
\item
  Write your answer as a fraction of an hour.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{15 minutes} b) \(\frac{15}{60} = \mathbf{\frac{1}{4}}\) of an
  hour
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

{Topic: Time and Fractions} {Skills: Fraction Simplification}

\end{exercise}

∑ × π ÷ √ ◆ ∞ ± ∫ ≠ Δ

\begin{exercise}[Savings and
Values]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u1-savings-perc}{}\label{exr-u1-savings-perc}

For every £200 Mrs.~Joy earns, she saves £34.

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  Work out £34 as a percentage of £200.\\
\item
  Last month she earned £1000. How much does she save?
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\tightlist
\item
  \(\frac{34}{200} \times 100 = \mathbf{17\%}\)\\
\item
  \(17\%\) of \(£1000 = 0.17 \times 1000 = \mathbf{£170}\)
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

{Topic: Savings} {Skills: Values as Percentages}

\end{exercise}

∑ × π ÷ √ ◆ ∞ ± ∫ ≠ Δ

\subsection{🔴 Challenging}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-important-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-important-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title={Multi-Step Reasoning}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\item
  Maryam works 8 hours a week and earns 50 QAR per hour. She decides to
  save \(\frac{2}{5}\) of her total weekly earnings. How many weeks will
  it take her to save 640 QAR?
\item
  There are 40 students in a class. \(\frac{3}{5}\) are girls.
  \(\frac{1}{4}\) of the girls wear glasses. How many girls in the class
  wear glasses?
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\alph{enumi})}
\item
  Weekly Pay: \(8 \times 50 = 400\)\\
  Weekly Savings: \((400 \div 5) \times 2 = 160\)\\
  Weeks needed: \(640 \div 160 = 4\) weeks
\item
  Total Girls: \((40 \div 5) \times 3 = 24\)\\
  Girls with glasses: \((24 \div 4) \times 1 = 6\)
\end{enumerate}

\end{tcolorbox}

{Topic: Fractions of Amounts}\\
{Skills: Logic \& Savings}

\section{⚡ Test Your Knowledge}\label{sec-ope-worksheet}

\chapter{Unit 2: Indices}\label{unit-2-indices}

\section{🎯 Learning Targets}\label{learning-targets-1}

LT1

Apply Multiplication Rules

Simplify expressions by adding powers when multiplying terms with the
same base.

{Same base} {Add exponents} {Index notation}

LT2

Apply Division Rules

Simplify expressions by subtracting powers when dividing terms with the
same base.

{Same base} {Subtract exponents} {Fraction form}

LT3

Master Power of a Power

Simplify expressions where a power is raised to another power by
multiplying the exponents.

{Brackets} {Multiply exponents} {Coefficients}

LT4

Manage Coefficients

Multiply or divide numerical coefficients separately from the algebraic
index laws.

{Separate coefficients} {Multiply \& divide} {Combined terms}

LT5

Handle Negative Indices

Correctly work with exponents when calculations produce or involve
negative indices.

{Negative exponents} {Reciprocal} {Sign rules}

LT6

Simplify Complex Fractions

Combine multiple index laws to simplify multi-step algebraic fractions
involving multiplication and division.

{Multi-step} {Mixed laws} {Algebraic fractions}

LT7

Operate with Surds

Add, subtract, multiply, and divide surd expressions, including those
with coefficients.

{Add \& subtract} {Multiply \& divide} {Like surds}

LT8

Simplify Surds

Express surds in simplest form by identifying and extracting perfect
square factors.

{Perfect squares} {Simplest form} {Prime factors}

LT9

Apply Surds

Rationalise denominators and solve problems that require exact surd
answers.

{Rationalise} {Exact values} {Problem solving}

\section{🗂️ Formula Card}\label{formula-card}

\subsection*{Algebraic Indices \& Surds}\label{algebraic-indices-surds}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsection}{Algebraic Indices \& Surds}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsubsection*{Laws of Indices --- The Core
Rules}\label{laws-of-indices-the-core-rules}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Laws of Indices --- The Core Rules}

\textbf{💡 Pro Tip} These rules ONLY apply when the \textbf{base} (the
big letter) is the same.

\textbf{Multiplication \& Division}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Multiplication}: Add the powers \(\rightarrow\)
  \[x^a \times x^b = x^{a+b}\]
\item
  \textbf{Division}: Subtract the powers \(\rightarrow\)
  \[\frac{x^a}{x^b} = x^{a-b}\]
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Examples}: \[y^5 \times y^3 = y^{5+3} = y^8\]
\[10w^7 \div 2w^3 = (10 \div 2)\,w^{7-3} = 5w^4\]

\subsubsection*{Power of a Power \& Zero}\label{power-of-a-power-zero}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Power of a Power \& Zero}

\textbf{🎯 Memory Trick} Brackets mean multiply!\\
Anything to the power of \(0\) is a hero (it becomes \(1\)).

\textbf{The Bracket Rule}: \[(x^a)^b = x^{a \times b} = x^{ab}\]

\textbf{Examples}: \[(k^3)^4 = k^{3 \times 4} = k^{12}\]
\[(5x^2)^3 = 5^3 \times x^{2 \times 3} = 125x^6\]

\textbf{The Zero Rule}: \[x^0 = 1\]

\subsubsection*{Negative \& Fractional
Indices}\label{negative-fractional-indices}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Negative \& Fractional Indices}

\textbf{⚠️ Common Mistake} A negative power does NOT make the number
negative; it makes it a reciprocal (fraction)!

\textbf{Negative Powers}: \[x^{-a} = \frac{1}{x^a}\]

\textbf{Fractional Powers}:
\[x^{\frac{1}{n}} = \sqrt[n]{x} \qquad x^{\frac{m}{n}} = \left(\sqrt[n]{x}\right)^m\]

\textbf{Examples}:
\[4^{-2} = \frac{1}{4^2} = \frac{1}{16} \qquad 9^{\frac{1}{2}} = \sqrt{9} = 3 \qquad 8^{\frac{2}{3}} = \left(\sqrt[3]{8}\right)^2 = 2^2 = 4\]

\subsubsection*{Expanding Brackets with
Indices}\label{expanding-brackets-with-indices}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Expanding Brackets with Indices}

\textbf{📝 Quick Method} Multiply the ``Big'' numbers (coefficients),
add the ``Small'' numbers (indices).

\textbf{Single Brackets}: \[a(b + c) = ab + ac\]

\textbf{Examples}:
\[3x^2(2x^3 + 4) = (3 \times 2)x^{2+3} + (3 \times 4)x^2 = 6x^5 + 12x^2\]
\[x^5(x^2 - x^{-3}) = x^{5+2} - x^{5-3} = x^7 - x^2\]

\subsubsection*{Algebraic Fractions with
Indices}\label{algebraic-fractions-with-indices}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Algebraic Fractions with Indices}

\textbf{Simplifying Fractions}:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Simplify the numerator (top) first using multiplication laws.
\item
  Simplify the denominator (bottom).
\item
  Use the division law (subtract) to find the final result.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Example}:
\[\frac{a^5 \times a^4}{a^2} = \frac{a^{9}}{a^2} = a^{9-2} = a^7\]

\textbf{Example with Coefficients}:
\[\frac{(2x^3)^2}{4x^4} = \frac{4x^6}{4x^4} = x^{6-4} = x^2\]

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsubsection*{Surds --- What is a Surd?}\label{surds-what-is-a-surd}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Surds --- What is a Surd?}

\textbf{💡 Definition} A \textbf{surd} is a root that cannot be written
as an exact fraction --- it is irrational.\\
\(\sqrt{2},\ \sqrt{3},\ \sqrt{5}\) are surds. \(\sqrt{4} = 2\) is
\textbf{not} a surd.\\
\textbf{Key fact}: \((\sqrt{a})^2 = a\) always.

\subsubsection*{Operating with Surds}\label{operating-with-surds}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Operating with Surds}

\textbf{🎯 Key Idea} You can only add or subtract surds with the
\textbf{same radicand}. Think of \(\sqrt{3}\) as a unit --- just like
\(3x + 5x = 8x\), we get \(3\sqrt{3} + 5\sqrt{3} = 8\sqrt{3}\).

\textbf{Addition \& Subtraction} --- collect like surds only:
\[a\sqrt{n} + b\sqrt{n} = (a+b)\sqrt{n} \qquad a\sqrt{n} - b\sqrt{n} = (a-b)\sqrt{n}\]

Unlike surds \textbf{cannot} be combined:
\(\quad 3\sqrt{2} + 5\sqrt{3}\) stays as is.

\textbf{Multiplication \& Division}:
\[\sqrt{a} \times \sqrt{b} = \sqrt{ab} \qquad \frac{\sqrt{a}}{\sqrt{b}} = \sqrt{\frac{a}{b}}\]
\[a\sqrt{m} \times b\sqrt{n} = ab\sqrt{mn}\]

\textbf{Examples}:
\[5\sqrt{7} - 10\sqrt{7} + 2\sqrt{3} = -5\sqrt{7} + 2\sqrt{3}\]
\[2\sqrt{10} \times 7\sqrt{6} = 14\sqrt{60} = 14\sqrt{4 \times 15} = 28\sqrt{15}\]

\subsubsection*{Simplifying Surds}\label{simplifying-surds}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Simplifying Surds}

\textbf{⚠️ Always} extract the \textbf{largest} perfect square factor.\\
\(\sqrt{72} = \sqrt{36 \times 2} = 6\sqrt{2}\) ✅ \(\quad\) not
\(2\sqrt{18}\) ✗

\textbf{Method} --- find largest perfect square \(k^2\) that divides
\(n\): \[\sqrt{n} = \sqrt{k^2 \times r} = k\sqrt{r}\]

\textbf{Steps}: find square factor → split → evaluate \(\sqrt{k^2} = k\)

\textbf{Examples}: \[\sqrt{200} = \sqrt{100 \times 2} = 10\sqrt{2}\]
\[3\sqrt{48} = 3 \times \sqrt{16 \times 3} = 3 \times 4\sqrt{3} = 12\sqrt{3}\]

\textbf{Perfect Squares}:
\(4,\ 9,\ 16,\ 25,\ 36,\ 49,\ 64,\ 81,\ 100,\ 121,\ 144,\ 169,\ 196,\ 225\)

\subsubsection*{Expanding \&
Rationalising}\label{expanding-rationalising}
\addcontentsline{toc}{subsubsection}{Expanding \& Rationalising}

\textbf{📝 Expanding} works exactly like algebra --- distribute every
term, use FOIL for double brackets, and remember \((\sqrt{a})^2 = a\).

\textbf{Single Bracket}:
\[\sqrt{a}(\sqrt{b} + c) = \sqrt{ab} + c\sqrt{a}\]

\textbf{Double Bracket (FOIL)}:
\[(\sqrt{a} + b)(\sqrt{a} + c) = a + (b+c)\sqrt{a} + bc\]

\textbf{Perfect Square}: \[(\sqrt{a} + b)^2 = a + 2b\sqrt{a} + b^2\]

\textbf{Conjugate Pair} --- always gives a rational result:
\[(\sqrt{a} + \sqrt{b})(\sqrt{a} - \sqrt{b}) = a - b\]

\textbf{Examples}: \[\sqrt{3}(\sqrt{3}+2) = 3 + 2\sqrt{3}\]
\[(\sqrt{5}+1)(\sqrt{5}-1) = 5-1 = 4\]
\[(\sqrt{2}+3)^2 = 2 + 6\sqrt{2} + 9 = 11 + 6\sqrt{2}\]

\textbf{Rationalising the Denominator} --- remove the surd from the
bottom.

\textbf{Simple}: multiply top and bottom by \(\sqrt{b}\):
\[\frac{a}{\sqrt{b}} \times \frac{\sqrt{b}}{\sqrt{b}} = \frac{a\sqrt{b}}{b}\]

\textbf{Binomial}: multiply by the \textbf{conjugate} of the
denominator:
\[\frac{a}{\sqrt{b}+c} \times \frac{\sqrt{b}-c}{\sqrt{b}-c} = \frac{a(\sqrt{b}-c)}{b-c^2}\]

The conjugate of \((\sqrt{b}+c)\) is \((\sqrt{b}-c)\) --- flip the sign
between the terms.

\textbf{Examples}:
\[\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}} = \frac{\sqrt{3}}{3} \qquad \frac{6}{\sqrt{2}} = \frac{6\sqrt{2}}{2} = 3\sqrt{2}\]

\[\frac{5}{\sqrt{3}+2} \times \frac{\sqrt{3}-2}{\sqrt{3}-2} = \frac{5(\sqrt{3}-2)}{3-4} = \frac{5(\sqrt{3}-2)}{-1} = 10-5\sqrt{3}\]

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle w^{2} \times w^{2}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle n^{3} \times n^{3}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle c^{7} \times c^{2}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle w^{7} \times w^{6}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle b^{6} \times b^{5}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle a^{2} \times a^{2}\)

\end{aligned}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-31}{}\label{exr-u2-31}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-32}{}\label{exr-u2-32}

\emph{Simplify.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle 10\sqrt{10} - 5\sqrt{10}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle 8\sqrt{10} - 4\sqrt{10}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle 7\sqrt{7} - 4\sqrt{7}\)

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-40}{}\label{exr-u2-40}

\emph{Simplify fully.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{640}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{700}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{28}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{468}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{208}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{1300}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{640}=\sqrt{64\times 10}=\sqrt{64}\times\sqrt{10}=8\sqrt{10}=8\sqrt{10}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{700}=\sqrt{100\times 7}=\sqrt{100}\times\sqrt{7}=10\sqrt{7}=10\sqrt{7}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{28}=\sqrt{4\times 7}=\sqrt{4}\times\sqrt{7}=2\sqrt{7}=2\sqrt{7}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{468}=\sqrt{36\times 13}=\sqrt{36}\times\sqrt{13}=6\sqrt{13}=6\sqrt{13}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{208}=\sqrt{16\times 13}=\sqrt{16}\times\sqrt{13}=4\sqrt{13}=4\sqrt{13}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{1300}=\sqrt{100\times 13}=\sqrt{100}\times\sqrt{13}=10\sqrt{13}=10\sqrt{13}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Perfect square recognition} {Surd simplification}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-12}{}\label{exr-u2-12}

\emph{Write as a single power by expressing each number as a prime
power.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle 8 \times 343\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle 16 \times 81\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle 25 \times 49\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle 25 \times 49\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle 9 \times 25\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle 8 \times 343\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
8\times 343=2^{3}\times 7^{3}=(2\times 7)^{3}=14^{3}=2744
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
16\times 81=2^{4}\times 3^{4}=(2\times 3)^{4}=6^{4}=1296
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
25\times 49=5^{2}\times 7^{2}=(5\times 7)^{2}=35^{2}=1225
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
25\times 49=5^{2}\times 7^{2}=(5\times 7)^{2}=35^{2}=1225
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
9\times 25=3^{2}\times 5^{2}=(3\times 5)^{2}=15^{2}=225
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
8\times 343=2^{3}\times 7^{3}=(2\times 7)^{3}=14^{3}=2744
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Prime factorisation} {Perfect square recognition} {Power distribution
law}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-13}{}\label{exr-u2-13}

\emph{Evaluate. Write as a fraction.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle 4^{-3}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle 7^{-2}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle 10^{-3}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle 3^{-3}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle 7^{-4}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle 4^{-1}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
4^{-3} = \dfrac{1}{4^{3}} = \dfrac{1}{64}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
7^{-2} = \dfrac{1}{7^{2}} = \dfrac{1}{49}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
10^{-3} = \dfrac{1}{10^{3}} = \dfrac{1}{1000}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3^{-3} = \dfrac{1}{3^{3}} = \dfrac{1}{27}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
7^{-4} = \dfrac{1}{7^{4}} = \dfrac{1}{2401}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
4^{-1} = \dfrac{1}{4^{1}} = \dfrac{1}{4}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Negative index as reciprocal} {Integer exponentiation} {Fraction
notation}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-14}{}\label{exr-u2-14}

\emph{Evaluate. Simplify your answer.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{2}{3}\right)^{-3}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{3}{4}\right)^{-2}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{2}{3}\right)^{-1}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{2}{5}\right)^{-1}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{2}{5}\right)^{-1}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{3}{4}\right)^{-3}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\dfrac{3}{2}\right)^{3}=\dfrac{3^{3}}{2^{3}}=\dfrac{27}{8}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\dfrac{4}{3}\right)^{2}=\dfrac{4^{2}}{3^{2}}=\dfrac{16}{9}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Flip: }\left(\dfrac{3}{2}\right)^{1}=\dfrac{3}{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Flip: }\left(\dfrac{5}{2}\right)^{1}=\dfrac{5}{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Flip: }\left(\dfrac{5}{2}\right)^{1}=\dfrac{5}{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\dfrac{4}{3}\right)^{3}=\dfrac{4^{3}}{3^{3}}=\dfrac{64}{27}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Negative index as reciprocal} {Fraction reciprocal}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-15}{}\label{exr-u2-15}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle y^{6} \times y^{-5}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle b^{2} \times b^{-4}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle p^{2} \times p^{-3}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle t^{6} \times t^{-4}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle y^{3} \times y^{-5}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle n^{4} \times n^{-5}\)

\end{aligned}

\textbf{f)}

\(\displaystyle \text{Write }\frac{1}{5}\text{ as a power of }5\)

\begin{aligned}

\end{aligned}

\textbf{d)}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-33}{}\label{exr-u2-33}

\emph{Simplify by collecting like surds.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle 7\sqrt{7}+6\sqrt{5}+5\sqrt{7}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle 3\sqrt{5}+4\sqrt{2}+2\sqrt{5}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle 4\sqrt{5}+2\sqrt{3}+5\sqrt{5}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle 2\sqrt{3}+2\sqrt{5}+5\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle 7\sqrt{5}+5\sqrt{3}+\sqrt{5}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle 5\sqrt{2}+5\sqrt{5}+4\sqrt{2}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}

\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(3+2)\sqrt{5}+4\sqrt{2}=5\sqrt{5}+4\sqrt{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(4+5)\sqrt{5}+2\sqrt{3}=9\sqrt{5}+2\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(2+5)\sqrt{3}+2\sqrt{5}=7\sqrt{3}+2\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(7+1)\sqrt{5}+5\sqrt{3}=8\sqrt{5}+5\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(5+4)\sqrt{2}+5\sqrt{5}=9\sqrt{2}+5\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Like surd identification} {Collecting like terms} {Integer addition}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-34}{}\label{exr-u2-34}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle 3\sqrt{5}+5\sqrt{3}-2\sqrt{5}-\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle 6\sqrt{2}+3\sqrt{7}-5\sqrt{2}-\sqrt{7}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle 3\sqrt{3}+4\sqrt{5}-\sqrt{3}-3\sqrt{5}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle 7\sqrt{7}+6\sqrt{3}-4\sqrt{7}-4\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle 5\sqrt{5}+7\sqrt{7}-\sqrt{5}-5\sqrt{7}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle 8\sqrt{2}+4\sqrt{3}-3\sqrt{2}-3\sqrt{3}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\end{aligned}

\end{aligned}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-36}{}\label{exr-u2-36}

\emph{Simplify.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle 3\sqrt{2} \times 5\sqrt{6}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle 5\sqrt{5} \times 2\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle 4\sqrt{5} \times 5\sqrt{2}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle 3\sqrt{5} \times 3\sqrt{6}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle 2\sqrt{7} \times 3\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle 4\sqrt{3} \times 2\sqrt{2}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3\times 5=15,\quad\sqrt{2}\times\sqrt{6}=\sqrt{12}=2\sqrt{3}\quad\Rightarrow30\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
5\times 2=10,\quad\sqrt{5}\times\sqrt{3}=\sqrt{15}=\sqrt{15}\quad\Rightarrow10\sqrt{15}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
4\times 5=20,\quad\sqrt{5}\times\sqrt{2}=\sqrt{10}=\sqrt{10}\quad\Rightarrow20\sqrt{10}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3\times 3=9,\quad\sqrt{5}\times\sqrt{6}=\sqrt{30}=\sqrt{30}\quad\Rightarrow9\sqrt{30}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
2\times 3=6,\quad\sqrt{7}\times\sqrt{3}=\sqrt{21}=\sqrt{21}\quad\Rightarrow6\sqrt{21}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
4\times 2=8,\quad\sqrt{3}\times\sqrt{2}=\sqrt{6}=\sqrt{6}\quad\Rightarrow8\sqrt{6}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Surd multiplication} {Coefficient multiplication} {Surd simplification}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-37}{}\label{exr-u2-37}

\emph{Simplify.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle 2\sqrt{3}\times 3\sqrt{3}\times 2\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle 3\sqrt{2}\times 2\sqrt{2}\times 2\sqrt{5}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle 3\sqrt{5}\times 2\sqrt{2}\times 3\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle 2\sqrt{3}\times 3\sqrt{3}\times 2\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle 2\sqrt{5}\times 3\sqrt{3}\times 2\sqrt{2}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle 2\sqrt{3}\times 2\sqrt{3}\times 3\sqrt{5}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}

\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3\times 2\times 2=12,\quad\sqrt{20}=2\sqrt{5}\quad\Rightarrow24\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3\times 2\times 3=18,\quad\sqrt{30}=\sqrt{30}\quad\Rightarrow18\sqrt{30}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
2\times 3\times 2=12,\quad\sqrt{27}=3\sqrt{3}\quad\Rightarrow36\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
2\times 3\times 2=12,\quad\sqrt{30}=\sqrt{30}\quad\Rightarrow12\sqrt{30}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
2\times 2\times 3=12,\quad\sqrt{45}=3\sqrt{5}\quad\Rightarrow36\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Surd multiplication} {Multi-step simplification}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-39}{}\label{exr-u2-39}

\emph{Simplify.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{6\sqrt{2}}{3\sqrt{2}}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{12\sqrt{20}}{3\sqrt{5}}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{9\sqrt{27}}{3\sqrt{3}}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{12\sqrt{12}}{3\sqrt{3}}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{8\sqrt{32}}{2\sqrt{2}}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{6\sqrt{20}}{2\sqrt{5}}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{6}{3}=2,\quad\dfrac{\sqrt{2}}{\sqrt{2}}=\sqrt{1}=1\quad\Rightarrow2
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{12}{3}=4,\quad\dfrac{\sqrt{20}}{\sqrt{5}}=\sqrt{4}=2\quad\Rightarrow8
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{9}{3}=3,\quad\dfrac{\sqrt{27}}{\sqrt{3}}=\sqrt{9}=3\quad\Rightarrow9
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{12}{3}=4,\quad\dfrac{\sqrt{12}}{\sqrt{3}}=\sqrt{4}=2\quad\Rightarrow8
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{8}{2}=4,\quad\dfrac{\sqrt{32}}{\sqrt{2}}=\sqrt{16}=4\quad\Rightarrow16
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{6}{2}=3,\quad\dfrac{\sqrt{20}}{\sqrt{5}}=\sqrt{4}=2\quad\Rightarrow6
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Surd division} {Coefficient division} {Surd simplification}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-41}{}\label{exr-u2-41}

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle 5\sqrt{12}\)

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-46}{}\label{exr-u2-46}

\emph{Expand and simplify.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{5}(\sqrt{7} + 5)\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{2}(2\sqrt{2} + 5)\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{6}(\sqrt{3} + 2)\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{3}(1\sqrt{3} + 4)\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{5}(\sqrt{3} + 5)\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle \sqrt{5}(2\sqrt{5} + 5)\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{35} + 5\sqrt{5} = \sqrt{35} + 5\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{2}\times 2\sqrt{2} + 5\sqrt{2} = 2\times 2 + 5\sqrt{2} = 4 + 5\sqrt{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{18} + 2\sqrt{6} = 3\sqrt{2} + 2\sqrt{6}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{3}\times 1\sqrt{3} + 4\sqrt{3} = 1\times 3 + 4\sqrt{3} = 3 + 4\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{15} + 5\sqrt{5} = \sqrt{15} + 5\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt{5}\times 2\sqrt{5} + 5\sqrt{5} = 2\times 5 + 5\sqrt{5} = 10 + 5\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Distributive law} {Surd multiplication} {Surd simplification}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-47}{}\label{exr-u2-47}

\emph{Expand and simplify.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{3} + 3)(\sqrt{3} + 4)\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{5} + 5)(\sqrt{5} - 4)\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{5} + 4)(\sqrt{5} - 5)\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{3} + 2)(\sqrt{3} + 5)\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{5} + 1)(\sqrt{5} - 4)\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{2} + 5)(\sqrt{2} - 1)\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
m + (a+b)\sqrt{m} + ab = 3 + 7\sqrt{3} + 12 = 15 + 7\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
m + (a+b)\sqrt{m} + ab = 5 + 1\sqrt{5} + -20 = -15 + 1\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
m + (a+b)\sqrt{m} + ab = 5 + -1\sqrt{5} + -20 = -15 - 1\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
m + (a+b)\sqrt{m} + ab = 3 + 7\sqrt{3} + 10 = 13 + 7\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
m + (a+b)\sqrt{m} + ab = 5 + -3\sqrt{5} + -4 = 1 - 3\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
m + (a+b)\sqrt{m} + ab = 2 + 4\sqrt{2} + -5 = -3 + 4\sqrt{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{FOIL method} {Surd multiplication} {Collecting like terms}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-49}{}\label{exr-u2-49}

\emph{Expand and simplify.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{7}+2)(\sqrt{7}-2)\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{11}+1)(\sqrt{11}-1)\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{6}+\sqrt{5})(\sqrt{6}-\sqrt{5})\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{6}+4)(\sqrt{6}-4)\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{13}+1)(\sqrt{13}-1)\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle (3\sqrt{2}+\sqrt{11})(3\sqrt{2}-\sqrt{11})\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\[
\begin{aligned}

\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(\sqrt{11})^2 - 1^2 = 11 - 1 = 10
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(\sqrt{6})^2 - (\sqrt{5})^2 = 1\times 6 - 5 = 6 - 5 = 1
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(\sqrt{6})^2 - 4^2 = 6 - 16 = -10
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(\sqrt{13})^2 - 1^2 = 13 - 1 = 12
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(3\sqrt{2})^2 - (\sqrt{11})^2 = 9\times 2 - 11 = 18 - 11 = 7
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Difference of squares} {Conjugate pairs} {Surd simplification}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-50}{}\label{exr-u2-50}

\subsection{🔴 Challenging}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-11}{}\label{exr-u2-11}

\emph{Simplify. Give your answer with positive exponents.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle (4w^{4})^{-3}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle (3x^{2})^{-3}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle (2x^{3})^{-2}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle (4c^{4})^{-2}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle (3k^{2})^{-1}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle (4k^{4})^{-1}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{1}{4^{3}w^{4\times 3}} = \dfrac{1}{64w^{12}}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{1}{3^{3}x^{2\times 3}} = \dfrac{1}{27x^{6}}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{1}{2^{2}x^{3\times 2}} = \dfrac{1}{4x^{6}}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{1}{4^{2}c^{4\times 2}} = \dfrac{1}{16c^{8}}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{1}{3^{1}k^{2\times 1}} = \dfrac{1}{3k^{2}}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{1}{4^{1}k^{4\times 1}} = \dfrac{1}{4k^{4}}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Power of power law} {Negative index as reciprocal} {Coefficient
exponentiation}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-18}{}\label{exr-u2-18}

\emph{Evaluate.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle 16^{\frac{2}{4}}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle 16^{\frac{2}{4}}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle 25^{\frac{4}{2}}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle 64^{\frac{2}{3}}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle 32^{\frac{4}{5}}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle 49^{\frac{3}{2}}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[4]{16}\right)^{2}=2^{2}=4
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[4]{16}\right)^{2}=2^{2}=4
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[2]{25}\right)^{4}=5^{4}=625
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[3]{64}\right)^{2}=4^{2}=16
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[5]{32}\right)^{4}=2^{4}=16
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[2]{49}\right)^{3}=7^{3}=343
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Fractional index as root and power} {nth root evaluation} {Integer
exponentiation}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-19}{}\label{exr-u2-19}

\emph{Evaluate.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle 256^{-\frac{3}{4}}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle 49^{-\frac{2}{2}}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle 256^{-\frac{3}{4}}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle 64^{-\frac{2}{3}}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle 256^{-\frac{3}{4}}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle 9^{-\frac{2}{2}}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
256^{-\frac{3}{4}} = \dfrac{1}{256^{\frac{3}{4}}}= \dfrac{1}{\left(\sqrt[4]{256}\right)^{3}}= \dfrac{1}{4^{3}} = \dfrac{1}{64}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
49^{-\frac{2}{2}} = \dfrac{1}{49^{\frac{2}{2}}}= \dfrac{1}{\left(\sqrt[2]{49}\right)^{2}}= \dfrac{1}{7^{2}} = \dfrac{1}{49}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
256^{-\frac{3}{4}} = \dfrac{1}{256^{\frac{3}{4}}}= \dfrac{1}{\left(\sqrt[4]{256}\right)^{3}}= \dfrac{1}{4^{3}} = \dfrac{1}{64}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
64^{-\frac{2}{3}} = \dfrac{1}{64^{\frac{2}{3}}}= \dfrac{1}{\left(\sqrt[3]{64}\right)^{2}}= \dfrac{1}{4^{2}} = \dfrac{1}{16}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
256^{-\frac{3}{4}} = \dfrac{1}{256^{\frac{3}{4}}}= \dfrac{1}{\left(\sqrt[4]{256}\right)^{3}}= \dfrac{1}{4^{3}} = \dfrac{1}{64}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
9^{-\frac{2}{2}} = \dfrac{1}{9^{\frac{2}{2}}}= \dfrac{1}{\left(\sqrt[2]{9}\right)^{2}}= \dfrac{1}{3^{2}} = \dfrac{1}{9}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Fractional index as root and power} {Negative index as reciprocal}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-20}{}\label{exr-u2-20}

\emph{Evaluate. Simplify your answer.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{27}{216}\right)^{\frac{3}{3}}\)

\textbf{b)}
\(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{125}{216}\right)^{\frac{1}{3}}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{64}{27}\right)^{\frac{2}{3}}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{27}{216}\right)^{\frac{2}{3}}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{4}{16}\right)^{\frac{3}{2}}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle \left(\dfrac{8}{27}\right)^{\frac{3}{3}}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[3]{\dfrac{27}{216}}\right)^{3}=\left(\dfrac{3}{6}\right)^{3}=\dfrac{3^{3}}{6^{3}}=\dfrac{1}{8}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[3]{\dfrac{125}{216}}\right)^{1}=\left(\dfrac{5}{6}\right)^{1}=\dfrac{5^{1}}{6^{1}}=\dfrac{5}{6}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[3]{\dfrac{64}{27}}\right)^{2}=\left(\dfrac{4}{3}\right)^{2}=\dfrac{4^{2}}{3^{2}}=\dfrac{16}{9}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[3]{\dfrac{27}{216}}\right)^{2}=\left(\dfrac{3}{6}\right)^{2}=\dfrac{3^{2}}{6^{2}}=\dfrac{1}{4}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[2]{\dfrac{4}{16}}\right)^{3}=\left(\dfrac{2}{4}\right)^{3}=\dfrac{2^{3}}{4^{3}}=\dfrac{1}{8}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\left(\sqrt[3]{\dfrac{8}{27}}\right)^{3}=\left(\dfrac{2}{3}\right)^{3}=\dfrac{2^{3}}{3^{3}}=\dfrac{8}{27}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Fractional index as root and power} {nth root of fraction}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-23}{}\label{exr-u2-23}

\emph{Simplify fully.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{3b^{4} \times 3b^{2}}{3b^{3}}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{4c^{3} \times 2c^{2}}{8c^{4}}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{3m^{2} \times 4m^{3}}{6m^{4}}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{3y^{2} \times 4y^{2}}{2y^{2}}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{3t^{5} \times 3t^{3}}{9t}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{3y^{3} \times 3y^{3}}{9y^{2}}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3\times 3=9,\;b^{4+2}=b^{6}\quad\dfrac{9}{3}=3,\;b^{6-3}=b^{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
4\times 2=8,\;c^{3+2}=c^{5}\quad\dfrac{8}{8}=1,\;c^{5-4}=c^{1}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3\times 4=12,\;m^{2+3}=m^{5}\quad\dfrac{12}{6}=2,\;m^{5-4}=m^{1}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3\times 4=12,\;y^{2+2}=y^{4}\quad\dfrac{12}{2}=6,\;y^{4-2}=y^{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3\times 3=9,\;t^{5+3}=t^{8}\quad\dfrac{9}{9}=1,\;t^{8-1}=t^{7}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3\times 3=9,\;y^{3+3}=y^{6}\quad\dfrac{9}{9}=1,\;y^{6-2}=y^{4}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Coefficient division} {Combining multiplication and division laws}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-24}{}\label{exr-u2-24}

\emph{Simplify fully.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{6a^{7}k^{6}}{2a^{3}k^{3}}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{12c^{2}w^{3}}{4cw^{2}}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{6c^{5}p^{3}}{3c^{2}p}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{6k^{6}x^{4}}{3k^{3}x^{2}}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{8k^{3}a^{5}}{2ka^{2}}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{4a^{3}b^{4}}{2a^{2}b}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{6}{2}=3,\quad a^{7-3}=a^{4},\quad k^{6-3}=k^{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{12}{4}=3,\quad c^{2-1}=c^{1},\quad w^{3-2}=w^{1}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{6}{3}=2,\quad c^{5-2}=c^{3},\quad p^{3-1}=p^{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{6}{3}=2,\quad k^{6-3}=k^{3},\quad x^{4-2}=x^{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{8}{2}=4,\quad k^{3-1}=k^{2},\quad a^{5-2}=a^{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{4}{2}=2,\quad a^{3-2}=a^{1},\quad b^{4-1}=b^{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Multi-variable expressions} {Coefficient division} {Multi-step
simplification}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-25}{}\label{exr-u2-25}

\emph{Simplify fully.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{c^{5} \times (c^{4})^{2}}{c^{10}}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{m^{5} \times (m^{4})^{3}}{m^{12}}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{c^{2} \times (c^{2})^{3}}{c}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{t^{2} \times (t^{3})^{3}}{t^{7}}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{m^{2} \times (m^{4})^{2}}{m^{2}}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{n^{2} \times (n^{4})^{2}}{n^{6}}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(c^{4})^{2}=c^{8},\quad c^{5}\times c^{8}=c^{13},\quad c^{13-10}=c^{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(m^{4})^{3}=m^{12},\quad m^{5}\times m^{12}=m^{17},\quad m^{17-12}=m^{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(c^{2})^{3}=c^{6},\quad c^{2}\times c^{6}=c^{8},\quad c^{8-1}=c^{7}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(t^{3})^{3}=t^{9},\quad t^{2}\times t^{9}=t^{11},\quad t^{11-7}=t^{4}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(m^{4})^{2}=m^{8},\quad m^{2}\times m^{8}=m^{10},\quad m^{10-2}=m^{8}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(n^{4})^{2}=n^{8},\quad n^{2}\times n^{8}=n^{10},\quad n^{10-6}=n^{4}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Power of power law} {Combining multiplication and division laws}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-29}{}\label{exr-u2-29}

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle (m^{5})^{\square} = m^{15}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\end{aligned}

\[
\begin{aligned}

\end{aligned}

\begin{aligned}

\end{aligned}

\end{aligned}

\textbf{f)}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-30}{}\label{exr-u2-30}

\emph{Identify the mistake and write the correct answer.}

A student wrote: \(27^{\frac{1}{3}} = 9\) (claiming
\(\frac{1}{3}\times27=9\))

\textbf{(a)} Identify the mistake.

\textbf{(b)} Write the correct answer.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
a^{\frac{1}{n}}=\sqrt[n]{a}\text{, not }\frac{1}{n}\times a
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sqrt[3]{27}=3
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Mathematical reasoning} {Error analysis} {Verbal mathematical
explanation}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-44}{}\label{exr-u2-44}

\emph{Simplify fully.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle 5\sqrt{3}+1\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle 2\sqrt{2}+4\sqrt{2}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle 2\sqrt{2}+2\sqrt{2}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle 3\sqrt{3}+4\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle 5\sqrt{3}+4\sqrt{3}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle 4\sqrt{3}+1\sqrt{3}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
5\times 1\sqrt{3}+1\times 1\sqrt{3}=(5+1)\sqrt{3}=6\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
2\times 1\sqrt{2}+4\times 1\sqrt{2}=(2+4)\sqrt{2}=6\sqrt{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
2\times 1\sqrt{2}+2\times 1\sqrt{2}=(2+2)\sqrt{2}=4\sqrt{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
3\times 1\sqrt{3}+4\times 1\sqrt{3}=(3+4)\sqrt{3}=7\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
5\times 1\sqrt{3}+4\times 1\sqrt{3}=(5+4)\sqrt{3}=9\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
4\times 1\sqrt{3}+1\times 1\sqrt{3}=(4+1)\sqrt{3}=5\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Surd simplification} {Collecting like terms} {Multi-step
simplification}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-45}{}\label{exr-u2-45}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-48}{}\label{exr-u2-48}

\emph{Expand and simplify.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{2} + 3)(2\sqrt{2} + 4)\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{2} + 4)(2\sqrt{2} + 4)\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle (2\sqrt{2} + 3)(\sqrt{2} - 1)\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{3} + 1)(2\sqrt{3} + 3)\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle (\sqrt{2} + 1)(2\sqrt{2} - 2)\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle (2\sqrt{5} + 4)(3\sqrt{5} + 1)\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
1\times 2\times 2=4,\quad(1\times 4+3\times 2)\sqrt{2}=10\sqrt{2},\quad\text{const}=12 \Rightarrow 16 + 10\sqrt{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
1\times 2\times 2=4,\quad(1\times 4+4\times 2)\sqrt{2}=12\sqrt{2},\quad\text{const}=16 \Rightarrow 20 + 12\sqrt{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
2\times 1\times 2=4,\quad(2\times -1+3\times 1)\sqrt{2}=1\sqrt{2},\quad\text{const}=-3 \Rightarrow 1 + 1\sqrt{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
1\times 2\times 3=6,\quad(1\times 3+1\times 2)\sqrt{3}=5\sqrt{3},\quad\text{const}=3 \Rightarrow 9 + 5\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
1\times 2\times 2=4,\quad(1\times -2+1\times 2)\sqrt{2}=0\sqrt{2},\quad\text{const}=-2 \Rightarrow 2
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
2\times 3\times 5=30,\quad(2\times 1+4\times 3)\sqrt{5}=14\sqrt{5},\quad\text{const}=4 \Rightarrow 34 + 14\sqrt{5}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{FOIL method} {Surd multiplication} {Collecting like terms}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-53}{}\label{exr-u2-53}

\emph{Rationalise the denominator and simplify.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{2}{\sqrt{3}+1}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{3}{\sqrt{2}+2}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{4}{\sqrt{7}+2}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{2}{\sqrt{5}+1}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{1}{\sqrt{5}+2}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{1}{\sqrt{5}+2}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{2}{\sqrt{3}+1}\times\dfrac{\sqrt{3}-1}{\sqrt{3}-1}=\dfrac{2(\sqrt{3}-1)}{3-1^2}=\dfrac{2(\sqrt{3}-1)}{2}=\sqrt{3}-1
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{3}{\sqrt{2}+2}\times\dfrac{\sqrt{2}-2}{\sqrt{2}-2}=\dfrac{3(\sqrt{2}-2)}{2-2^2}=\dfrac{3(\sqrt{2}-2)}{-2}=-\dfrac{3(\sqrt{2}-2)}{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{4}{\sqrt{7}+2}\times\dfrac{\sqrt{7}-2}{\sqrt{7}-2}=\dfrac{4(\sqrt{7}-2)}{7-2^2}=\dfrac{4(\sqrt{7}-2)}{3}=\dfrac{4(\sqrt{7}-2)}{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{2}{\sqrt{5}+1}\times\dfrac{\sqrt{5}-1}{\sqrt{5}-1}=\dfrac{2(\sqrt{5}-1)}{5-1^2}=\dfrac{2(\sqrt{5}-1)}{4}=\dfrac{1(\sqrt{5}-1)}{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{1}{\sqrt{5}+2}\times\dfrac{\sqrt{5}-2}{\sqrt{5}-2}=\dfrac{1(\sqrt{5}-2)}{5-2^2}=\dfrac{1(\sqrt{5}-2)}{1}=\sqrt{5}-2
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{1}{\sqrt{5}+2}\times\dfrac{\sqrt{5}-2}{\sqrt{5}-2}=\dfrac{1(\sqrt{5}-2)}{5-2^2}=\dfrac{1(\sqrt{5}-2)}{1}=\sqrt{5}-2
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Conjugate pairs} {Difference of squares} {Rationalise denominator}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-54}{}\label{exr-u2-54}

\emph{Rationalise the denominator fully and simplify.}

Rationalise the denominator: \(\dfrac{4+\sqrt{5}}{\sqrt{7}-3}\)

\textbf{(a)} State the conjugate of the denominator.

\textbf{(b)} Multiply numerator and denominator by the conjugate and
simplify.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Conjugate of }(\sqrt{7}-3)\text{ is }(\sqrt{7}+3)
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{(4+\sqrt{5})(\sqrt{7}+3)}{(\sqrt{7})^2-3^2}=\dfrac{4\sqrt{7}+12+\sqrt{35}+3\sqrt{5}}{-2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Conjugate pairs} {Difference of squares} {Multi-step rationalisation}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-55}{}\label{exr-u2-55}

\emph{Rationalise each denominator and add.}

Rationalise and simplify:
\(\dfrac{2}{\sqrt{3}-1}+\dfrac{2}{3-\sqrt{3}}\)

\textbf{(a)} Rationalise each fraction separately.

\textbf{(b)} Add the simplified fractions together.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{2}{\sqrt{3}-1}\times\dfrac{\sqrt{3}+1}{\sqrt{3}+1}=\dfrac{2(\sqrt{3}+1)}{2}=\sqrt{3}+1 \\ \dfrac{2}{3-\sqrt{3}}\times\dfrac{3+\sqrt{3}}{3+\sqrt{3}}=\dfrac{2(3+\sqrt{3})}{6}=\dfrac{3+\sqrt{3}}{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(\sqrt{3}+1)+\dfrac{3+\sqrt{3}}{3}=\dfrac{3\sqrt{3}+3+3+\sqrt{3}}{3}=\dfrac{4\sqrt{3}+6}{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Rationalise denominator} {Adding fractions} {Multi-step simplification}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-56}{}\label{exr-u2-56}

\emph{Rationalise and simplify.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{\sqrt{12}+6}{\sqrt{3}}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{\sqrt{12}+6}{\sqrt{3}}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{\sqrt{18}+10}{\sqrt{2}}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{\sqrt{12}+6}{\sqrt{3}}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{\sqrt{50}+10}{\sqrt{2}}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle \dfrac{\sqrt{12}+6}{\sqrt{3}}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{\sqrt{12}}{\sqrt{3}}+\dfrac{6}{\sqrt{3}}=\sqrt{4}+\dfrac{6\sqrt{3}}{3}=2+2\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{\sqrt{12}}{\sqrt{3}}+\dfrac{6}{\sqrt{3}}=\sqrt{4}+\dfrac{6\sqrt{3}}{3}=2+2\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{\sqrt{18}}{\sqrt{2}}+\dfrac{10}{\sqrt{2}}=\sqrt{9}+\dfrac{10\sqrt{2}}{2}=3+5\sqrt{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{\sqrt{12}}{\sqrt{3}}+\dfrac{6}{\sqrt{3}}=\sqrt{4}+\dfrac{6\sqrt{3}}{3}=2+2\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{\sqrt{50}}{\sqrt{2}}+\dfrac{10}{\sqrt{2}}=\sqrt{25}+\dfrac{10\sqrt{2}}{2}=5+5\sqrt{2}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\dfrac{\sqrt{12}}{\sqrt{3}}+\dfrac{6}{\sqrt{3}}=\sqrt{4}+\dfrac{6\sqrt{3}}{3}=2+2\sqrt{3}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Splitting fractions} {Rationalise denominator} {Surd simplification}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-57}{}\label{exr-u2-57}

\emph{Find the values of x and y.}

\textbf{a)} \(\displaystyle (3-\sqrt{x})^2 = y - 6\sqrt{2}\)

\textbf{b)} \(\displaystyle (7-\sqrt{x})^2 = y - 14\sqrt{2}\)

\textbf{c)} \(\displaystyle (3-\sqrt{x})^2 = y - 6\sqrt{2}\)

\textbf{d)} \(\displaystyle (5-\sqrt{x})^2 = y - 10\sqrt{2}\)

\textbf{e)} \(\displaystyle (6-\sqrt{x})^2 = y - 12\sqrt{2}\)

\textbf{f)} \(\displaystyle (5-\sqrt{x})^2 = y - 10\sqrt{2}\)

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solutions}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(3)^2-6\sqrt{x}+x \Rightarrow x=2,\; y=9+2=11
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(7)^2-14\sqrt{x}+x \Rightarrow x=2,\; y=49+2=51
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{c)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(3)^2-6\sqrt{x}+x \Rightarrow x=2,\; y=9+2=11
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{d)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(5)^2-10\sqrt{x}+x \Rightarrow x=2,\; y=25+2=27
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{e)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(6)^2-12\sqrt{x}+x \Rightarrow x=2,\; y=36+2=38
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{f)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
(5)^2-10\sqrt{x}+x \Rightarrow x=2,\; y=25+2=27
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Coefficient matching} {Surd expansion} {Algebraic reasoning}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-58}{}\label{exr-u2-58}

\emph{Use Pythagoras' theorem. Give your answer as a simplified surd.}

The diagram shows a right-angled triangle with hypotenuse \(\sqrt{31}\)
and one leg \(\sqrt{22}\).

\textbf{(a)} Find the exact value of \(x\). Give your answer in simplest
surd form.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
x^2 = (\sqrt{31})^2 - (\sqrt{22})^2 = 31 - 22 = 9 \\ x = \sqrt{9} = 3
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Pythagoras theorem} {Surd simplification} {Surd arithmetic}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-u2-59}{}\label{exr-u2-59}

\emph{Show your working clearly.}

A trapezium has parallel sides of length \(4\) cm and \(k\) cm, a
perpendicular height of \(\sqrt{3}\) cm, and an area of \(5\sqrt{6}\)
cm².

\textbf{(a)} Show that \(k = 10\sqrt{2}-4\).

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\frac{(4+k)\sqrt{3}}{2}=5\sqrt{6} \\ 4+k=10\sqrt{2} \\ k=10\sqrt{2}-4
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Area formula} {Surd division} {Rationalise denominator} {Multi-step
simplification}

\end{exercise}
