\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-13}{}\label{exr-trig-13}

\emph{Use trigonometry to find the unknown measurement. Give your answer
to 2 decimal places.}

A person stands 50 m from a vertical tower. The angle of elevation to
the top is 55°.

\textbf{(a)} Find the height of the tower.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\tan 55° = \dfrac{h}{50} \\ h = 50 \times \tan 55° \\ h = 71.41 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Elevation diagram} {tan ratio} {Real-world modelling}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-14}{}\label{exr-trig-14}

\emph{Use trigonometry to find the unknown measurement. Give your answer
to 2 decimal places.}

An observer at the top of a 40 m cliff looks down at a boat with angle
of depression 30°.

\textbf{(a)} Find the horizontal distance from the cliff base to the
boat.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\tan 30° = \dfrac{40}{d} \\ d = \dfrac{40}{\tan 30°} \\ d = 69.28 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Depression diagram} {tan ratio} {Alternate angles}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-17}{}\label{exr-trig-17}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

A flagpole casts a shadow of 5.72 m when the angle of elevation to the
sun is 65°.

\textbf{(a)} Find the height of the flagpole.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\tan 65° = \dfrac{h}{5.72} \\ h = 5.72 \times \tan 65° = 12.27 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{tan ratio} {Shadow geometry} {Real-world modelling}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-18}{}\label{exr-trig-18}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

A hill is inclined at 12° to the horizontal, base at sea level.

\textbf{(a)} If you walk 150 m up the hill, what is your height above
sea level?

\textbf{(b)} If you climb to 80 m above sea level, how far have you
walked?

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
h = 150 \sin 12° = 31.19 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sin 12° = \dfrac{80}{d} \\ d = \dfrac{80}{\sin 12°} = 384.78 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{sin for height} {cos for horizontal} {Hill geometry}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-19}{}\label{exr-trig-19}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

A train climbs 6.4 m for every 150 m of track.

\textbf{(a)} Find the angle of incline.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\sin\theta = \dfrac{6.4}{150} \\ \theta = \sin^{-1}\!\left(\dfrac{6.4}{150}\right) = 2.4°
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{sin⁻¹} {Gradient geometry} {Small angles}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-20}{}\label{exr-trig-20}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 1 decimal place.}

A 65 m building. Point \(A\) is 113 m from its base.

\textbf{(a)} Find the angle of elevation from A to the top of the
building.

\textbf{(b)} What is the angle of depression from the top to A?

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\tan\theta = \dfrac{65}{113} \\ \theta = \tan^{-1}\!\left(\dfrac{65}{113}\right) = 29.9°
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Depression angle} = \text{elevation angle} = 29.9° \\ \text{(Alternate interior angles with horizontal)}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Elevation angle} {Depression angle} {Alternate angles}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-21}{}\label{exr-trig-21}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

The handle is held 85 cm above the ground. The string is 10 m long at
55° to the horizontal.

\textbf{Given:} \text{String} = 10\text{ m} · \text{Angle} = 55° ·
\text{Handle} = 85\text{ cm}

\textbf{(a)} Calculate the height of the kite above the ground.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Vertical} = 10 \sin 55° = 8.19 \text{ m} \\ \text{Handle} = 85 \text{ cm} = 0.85 \text{ m} \\ \text{Total} = 8.19 + 0.85 = 9.04 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{sin ratio} {Height calculation} {Unit conversion}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-24}{}\label{exr-trig-24}

\emph{Show all working. Give angles to 1 decimal place.}

A ladder leans against a wall. Wall height = 5.6 m, base distance = 0.9
m. Safe angle: 70°--80° to the ground.

\textbf{(a)} Is the ladder safe? Show your working.

\textbf{(b)} Calculate the length of the ladder.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\tan\theta = \dfrac{5.6}{0.9} \\ \theta = \tan^{-1}\!\left(\dfrac{5.6}{0.9}\right) = 80.9° \\ 80.9° \text{ is NOT safe (outside 70°–80°)}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
L^2 = 5.6^2 + 0.9^2 = 32.17 \\ L = \sqrt{32.17} = 5.67 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{tan ratio} {Angle calculation} {Safety constraint}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-25}{}\label{exr-trig-25}

\emph{Convert units where needed. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

A ramp: horizontal distance 2.0 m, height 20 cm.

\textbf{(a)} Calculate the size of angle \(y\).

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Convert: } 20 \text{ cm} = 0.2 \text{ m} \\ \tan y = \dfrac{0.2}{2.0} \\ y = \tan^{-1}\!\left(\dfrac{0.2}{2.0}\right) = 5.7°
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Unit conversion} {tan⁻¹} {Ramp geometry}

\end{exercise}

∑ × π ÷ √ ◆ ∞ ± ∫ ≠ Δ

\subsection{🔴 Challenging}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-15}{}\label{exr-trig-15}

\emph{Draw a diagram, label all measurements, and find the answer. Give
your answer to 2 decimal places.}

A tree of height 20 m is observed at an angle of elevation of 40° from
the ground.

\textbf{(a)} Draw and label a diagram.

\textbf{(b)} Find the horizontal distance to 2 d.p.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Vertical = height, horizontal = distance, }\theta\text{ at base}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\tan 40° = \dfrac{20}{d} \\ d = \dfrac{20}{\tan 40°} \\ d = 23.84 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Problem decomposition} {Diagram construction} {tan ratio}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-16}{}\label{exr-trig-16}

\emph{Draw a diagram, label all measurements, and find the answer. Give
your answer to 2 decimal places.}

A drone hovers 20 m above ground. Angle of depression to a landmark is
30°.

\textbf{(a)} Draw and label a diagram.

\textbf{(b)} Find the horizontal distance to 2 d.p.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Horizontal line at top; depression angle = interior angle}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Depression angle} = 30° \text{ (alternate angles)} \\ \tan 30° = \dfrac{20}{d} \\ d = \dfrac{20}{\tan 30°} = 34.64 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Problem decomposition} {Diagram construction} {Alternate angles}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-22}{}\label{exr-trig-22}

\emph{Show all working clearly. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

Two points A and B on opposite sides of a tower. From A: elevation 30°,
distance 15 m. From B: elevation 35°.

\textbf{(a)} Find the height of the tower.

\textbf{(b)} Find the horizontal distance from B to the tower.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
h = 15 \times \tan 30° = 8.66 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
d_B = \dfrac{8.66}{\tan 35°} = 12.37 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Multi-step reasoning} {Shared side} {Combined trig}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-23}{}\label{exr-trig-23}

\emph{Show all working clearly. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

A ship sails 12 km on bearing 060°.

\textbf{(a)} How far north of port is the ship?

\textbf{(b)} How far east of port is the ship?

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
N = 12 \cos 60° = 6 \text{ km}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
E = 12 \sin 60° = 10.39 \text{ km}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Bearing interpretation} {North reference} {Multi-step trig}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-26}{}\label{exr-trig-26}

\emph{Show all working clearly. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

Two right-angled triangles share side BD.

\textbf{Given:} AB=8\text{ cm} · BC=2\text{ cm} · \angle BCD=55°

\textbf{(a)} Calculate angle \(ABD\) (marked \(x\)).

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\triangle BCD: \quad BD = BC \times \tan 55° = 2 \times \tan 55° = 2.86 \text{ cm} \\ \triangle ABD: \quad \sin(x) = \dfrac{2.86}{8} \\ x = \sin^{-1}\!\left(\dfrac{2.86}{8}\right) = 20.9°
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Multi-step reasoning} {Vertex labelling} {Combined trig}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-27}{}\label{exr-trig-27}

\emph{Show all working clearly. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

Right-angled triangles ABD and BCD share side BD.

\textbf{Given:} AB=16\text{ cm} · \angle ABD=70° ·
\angle ABD:\angle DBC=5:2

\textbf{(a)} Work out the length of \(CD\).

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\angle DBC = \dfrac{2}{5} \times 70° = 28.0° \\ BD = 16 \sin 70° = 15.04 \text{ cm} \\ CD = BD \times \tan 28.0° = 15.04 \times \tan 28.0° = 8 \text{ cm}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Ratio splitting} {Multi-step trig} {Angle arithmetic}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-28}{}\label{exr-trig-28}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 1 decimal place.}

Isosceles triangle \(FLG\): \(FL = LG = 32\) cm, \(FG = 20\) cm.

\textbf{(a)} Work out angle \(LFG\).

\textbf{(b)} Work out angle \(FLG\).

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Drop perpendicular from L to midpoint M of FG} \\ FM = \dfrac{20}{2} = 10.0 \text{ cm} \\ \sin(\angle LFG) = \dfrac{10.0}{32} \\ \angle LFG = \sin^{-1}\!\left(\dfrac{10.0}{32}\right) = 18.2°
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\angle FLG = 180° - 2 \times 18.2° = 143.6°
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Isosceles properties} {Perpendicular bisector} {sin application}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-29}{}\label{exr-trig-29}

\emph{Show all working. Give bearing to nearest degree.}

A helicopter flies 10 km due east, then 6 km due north.

\textbf{(a)} Find the direct distance.

\textbf{(b)} Calculate the bearing.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
d^2 = 10^2 + 6^2 = 136 \\ d = \sqrt{136} = 11.66 \text{ km}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\tan\theta = \dfrac{10}{6} \\ \theta = \tan^{-1}\!\left(\dfrac{10}{6}\right) = 59.0° \\ \text{Bearing} = 059°
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Pythagoras} {tan⁻¹ for bearing} {Compass directions}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-30}{}\label{exr-trig-30}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

A boat approaches a 120 m cliff with a 25 m lighthouse on top. Angle of
elevation to top of lighthouse is 20°.

\textbf{Given:} \text{Cliff} = 120\text{ m} · \text{Lighthouse} =
25\text{ m} · \text{Elevation to lighthouse top} = 20°

\textbf{(a)} Find the distance from the boat to the base of the cliff.

\textbf{(b)} Find the angle of elevation from the boat to the top of the
cliff.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\tan 20° = \dfrac{145}{d} \\ d = \dfrac{145}{\tan 20°} = 398.38 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\textbf{b)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\tan\alpha = \dfrac{120}{398.38} \\ \alpha = \tan^{-1}\!\left(\dfrac{120}{398.38}\right) = 16.8°
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Multi-step trig} {Total height} {Elevation angles}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-31}{}\label{exr-trig-31}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

A chord of 5.3 cm subtends an angle of 34° at the centre.

\textbf{Given:} \text{Chord} = 5.3\text{ cm} · \text{Angle at centre} =
34°

\textbf{(a)} Find the radius of the circle.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Half-chord} = \dfrac{5.3}{2} = 2.65 \text{ cm} \\ \sin 34° = \dfrac{2.65}{r} \\ r = \dfrac{2.65}{\sin 34°} = 4.74 \text{ cm}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Circle geometry} {sin ratio} {Right triangle in circle}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-32}{}\label{exr-trig-32}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

From 200 m away: elevation to flagpole bottom = 34°, to top = 38°.

\textbf{(a)} Find the height of the flagpole.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
h_1 = 200 \tan 34° = 134.9 \text{ m} \\ h_2 = 200 \tan 38° = 156.26 \text{ m} \\ \text{Flagpole} = 156.26 - 134.9 = 21.36 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Multi-step trig} {Two-angle setup} {Subtraction}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-33}{}\label{exr-trig-33}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

Depression from top of 18 m cliff: first 3.3°, then 5.5°. How far does
the boat move?

\textbf{(a)} How much closer must the boat move?

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
d_1 = \dfrac{18}{\tan 3.3°} = 312.18 \text{ m} \\ d_2 = \dfrac{18}{\tan 5.5°} = 186.94 \text{ m} \\ \text{Moved} = 312.18 - 186.94 = 125.24 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Two depression angles} {Distance difference} {Multi-step trig}

\end{exercise}

\begin{exercise}[]\protect\hypertarget{exr-trig-34}{}\label{exr-trig-34}

\emph{Show all working. Give your answer to 2 decimal places.}

Helicopter at 90 km/h. Takes 15 s to go from overhead to elevation angle
65°.

\textbf{(a)} Find the height of the helicopter.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, arc=.35mm, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, colback=white, bottomrule=.15mm, left=2mm, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, titlerule=0mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{🔍 View Solution}, leftrule=.75mm, breakable, rightrule=.15mm, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, toprule=.15mm]

\textbf{a)}

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{Distance} = 90 \times \dfrac{15}{3600} = 0.38 \text{ km} \\ h = 0.38 \times \tan 65° = 0.81 \text{ km} \\ h = 810 \text{ m}
\end{aligned}
\]

\end{tcolorbox}

{Speed-distance-time} {tan ratio} {Unit conversion}

\end{exercise}

∑ × π ÷ √ ◆ ∞ ± ∫ ≠ Δ
